Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

Clenching Our Teeth 209

— Yang An

As a reporter traveling in Qingdao, I visited the Fourth Iron Exhibition. The exhibits from each pavilion were extremely rich, and I deeply rejoice that China has boundless hope for the future. After visiting the sales office, the scene in front of the door was deserted, no longer like the scene in the previous session in Peiping. I began to lament that the current people's purchasing power is unexpectedly weak, and I felt that I was being bound and restrained everywhere, and I didn't know whether to laugh or cry, and I was extremely heartbroken! It is unfortunate to be born in this world. Even the slogan of "Promoting National Goods" will be silenced by someone, and no publicity will be allowed. How can one not be saddened? However, since the situation is like this, there is no other way. Everyone must clench their teeth and work hard, and there will be a day when we can breathe a sigh of relief. From now on, whether it is a manufacturing factory or a sales store, for national goods, we can only work hard on the ground. We, the common people, can only follow them and do what we can. We don't have to rush for quick success, and we don't have to talk endlessly. It is just a matter of clenching our teeth, swallowing our blood, and fighting for honor.

In this extremely difficult era, national goods industrialists should not be overly pessimistic and simply be passive, nor should they be vain and arrogant and take it lightly. For everything, we can only achieve "drinking tears and containing sorrow", and wait quietly for the day to come again. Small setbacks need not be discouraged, and all kinds of difficulties and hardships may not be the old heaven to achieve you. What is especially important is to know yourself and your enemy. To know your enemy, you must first know yourself. Knowing your own weaknesses, you can then achieve something. Knowing the strengths of others, you can then learn from them. The way out for the national goods industry is here.

The Establishment of the Industrial and Commercial Revival Association and the Future of National Goods 210

— Xuan Wan

We have examined the trends of the national goods movement in recent years, and it has gradually moved from the theoretical to the practical stage. Many people are working hard and making efforts to move forward. This is indeed a good phenomenon to save the current economic crisis in our country. The "Industrial and Commercial Revival Committee" initiated by the city's chamber of commerce and jointly organized by the industrial and commercial circles has been formally established and has issued a declaration and work outline. It can make us believe even more that under the urgent phenomenon of the industrial crisis, the emergence of this committee has the greatest significance for the development of the future of national goods, because the industrial management and production technology neglected by our country's industrial circles in the past are undoubtedly the main reason for hindering the progress of the entire cause. The association is now advocating how to improve industrial technology and management methods, which will indeed give the industrial and commercial circles a new opportunity for revival and progress.

As everyone knows, our country is originally a country with backward production. Therefore, industrial organization, management methods, and production technology cannot compete with foreigners, and the progress of the industry has also suffered great difficulties. However, here, we must never be discouraged. We must know that our country's current production rate and consumption rate are only in a ratio of two to five. Therefore, the emergence of new industries and the adaptation of mechanized products to the needs of the public are precisely driven by historical conditions. We only need to recognize that Chinese industry has suffered losses in organization and technology in the past. From now on, we will seek to improve industrial technology and sales methods from here, and investigate the main reasons for the decline of various industries, and give appropriate remedies. This scientific attitude and the conscious performance of the industrial and commercial circles are the best and most correct phenomena.

However, at the beginning of the association's establishment, in my personal opinion, there are still a few practical issues worthy of discussion that should be put forward for discussion and hope that the public will pay attention to. That is, first, I hope that the association can further expand and improve its own organization, and hire industry leaders, or people with rich knowledge and experience, to jointly study and seek the development of the industrial and commercial circles in the future, so as to be competent for this arduous task. Second, we must conduct a detailed survey of the industrial situation of industrial advanced countries in the world, and refer to their organization and technology in a certain industry, and draft a standard plan for improvement that is suitable for our country, so as to prepare for the reform and practice of various industries in the future. Third, after the investigation, we must take an active attitude and do our best to guide various industries with the research results and design improvement methods that have been achieved, and implement them in a practical manner. In this way, I think the recession in the entire industrial and commercial circles will surely turn from the abyss of near bankruptcy to the bright right track.

Rational Summer Supplies 211

— Ba Ling

The wheels of the era are following the track of time, and some are not lazy in the past. Now, it is already the summer when the fire umbrella is high and the heat waves are hitting. In summer, our daily necessities, food, and clothing are naturally different from other seasons. There are some small changes. To be clear, people are indeed very cautious about summer supplies. How to purchase rational summer supplies has become a problem worth discussing. Regarding this issue, it seems that someone in this publication has talked about it, but in my opinion, it still feels slightly brief and not detailed enough. Now, I will express some simple opinions on how to rationalize summer supplies according to my views below:

First, I think rational summer supplies should naturally be national goods. We are Chinese, and we should purchase Chinese goods. Whether it is winter or summer, we should purchase national goods for our living needs throughout the year, 365 days a year. In this way, the national goods industry will develop, the national goods movement will succeed, the national economy will be prosperous, and rural bankruptcy can be saved. During this summer, our supplies are naturally more than other seasons. I sincerely advise my fellow compatriots who purchase summer supplies to firmly remember the words "national goods", so that we will be able to recover a lot of rights and interests, which is of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood.

Second, I think rational summer supplies should be durable. Everyone knows that the difference between durable supplies and non-durable supplies is very large. Some people buy a shirt that can be worn for three summers. However, some people buy a shirt that can only be worn for one summer. What is the difference between being cheap and being at a disadvantage? It goes without saying. Therefore, when we purchase summer supplies, we should go to famous national goods factories to buy them. For example, for towel quilts, we should go to Sanyou Industrial Company to buy them. For shirts, we should go to Wuhe or Jinglun to buy them. For straw hats, we should go to Huafu Zhenxing to buy them. We cannot lack this common sense, because the products of famous national goods factories seem to be slightly more expensive on the surface, but after buying them, they are much more durable than ordinary ones. We should understand this inherent cheapness.

Third, I want to talk about summer drinks. In summer, people's consumption of drinks is also very large, but some people like to eat foreign drinks, which is very painful. You must know that the drink industry in our China is now making rapid progress compared to the past. For example, the fruit dew of Guanshengyuan, the Family Industrial Cooperative, and the Taikang Canned Food Company, the soda of Yili, the fresh milk of Shengsheng, and ice cream, etc., are their manufacturing processes clean and hygienic? What are the shortcomings of foreign goods? Therefore, here, I would like to sincerely advise my fellow compatriots that we should still use our own national goods for summer drinks. You must know that when you eat foreign drinks, you always feel a little uneasy in your heart. When you eat Chinese drinks, the rights and interests will not flow out, and how comfortable and at ease is the spirit?

The above three small opinions are my contribution to my fellow compatriots who purchase summer supplies. I don't know if my humble opinion can get some sympathy?

Promoting National Goods is the Responsibility of a Virtuous Wife 212

— Lan Shan

Since his marriage, my old friend Mr. Yang has changed a lot. His change is considered rare, but it is all due to his wife, Ms. Liu's, powerful performance of both soft and hard skills.

Mr. Yang is twenty-eight years old this year and works in the transportation department, with a good monthly income. He married Ms. Liu, a high-achieving student from Chongde Women's School, who is twenty-two years old, in March of this year. Mr. Yang used to be a Western-style friend, with fashionable clothes. Almost everything he needed was selected from imported goods, from the felt hats and straw hats on his head to the hair water and sedan Kang, and down to the patterned socks and leather shoes. They were all authentic imports, because he thought that national goods could not satisfy people. However, since his marriage, he has not bought any more Western suits. This summer, he wears silk gauze and small boat long gowns and short shirts and trousers. The shoes are gauze shoes, white socks, and a national goods straw hat. When I first saw him, I really couldn't recognize him. Since I met him, I had never seen him wear Chinese clothes. At this time, he was graceful, gentle and refined, and looked better than when he wore a suit. However, I finally asked him: "Oh, Ah Yang! What's wrong? You've also changed your style!"

"Actually, Chinese shirts are much more comfortable to wear! And they are also very cool."

"But what is the motive for you to change to Chinese clothes?" I asked.

"It's patriotism!" His face turned a little red. "My woman insisted that I change to Chinese clothes, saying that this way I can promote national goods. She also told me not to buy any more Western suits in the future, saying that I don't look good in Western suits, and the raw materials are mostly from foreign countries, which makes people earn our money."

"She is indeed patriotic, but what kind of cloth does she wear herself?"

"It's all Chinese fabrics. She opposes buying any beautiful foreign yarn. Not only are the clothes like this, but even the cosmetics are not foreign. She doesn't use "White Man" head water, "4711" perfume, or "Three Flowers Brand" flour and rouge. She only buys cheap and good-quality national goods."

"That's it. Your wife is definitely more sensible than you."

"Sensible is sensible, but she is also too meticulous. When she gets something in her hands, she has to ask if it is Chinese goods, like an inspection committee member. The things used at home are limited to me to buy Chinese goods. If it is a foreign product, it is not allowed to enter the door, and she wants me to take it back to return it at night, with no room for discussion. Now all the things used at home have been handled entirely by her."

I have visited his house several times. Except for a foreign wardrobe that Mr. Yang bought in the past, a dozen sets of Western suits, two pairs of old foreign leather shoes, a raincoat, and a phonograph, I can't find any other foreign goods. I really praised Mrs. Yang a few words, and she also invited me to drink a bottle of national goods soda.

I really admire Mrs. Yang more and more. In this Shanghai beach, where vanity is especially important, women (especially educated women) tend to admire Westernization and become powerful users of foreign goods. Mrs. Yang has corrected this problem, set an example, influenced her husband, and fulfilled a little of the national duty. She is truly a 100% virtuous wife!

I wrote this article with the consent of Mr. and Mrs. Yang. I hope that many wives will come up with good ideas and tricks to influence those Westernized husbands. If you also like to use foreign goods, then wake up immediately and take Mrs. Yang as a model. If it is not a national product, you are not allowed to bring it into the house. If everyone can really implement this, the Chinese national goods industry will have a savior, and the Chinese economic crisis can be avoided. From today, I wish many women to be determined to be a virtuous wife who knows the times!

A Record of Visiting the China Enamel Factory 213

— Wu Ya

If you pay attention to the trademarks of the enamelware sold on the market, you will definitely see the Lihuo brand porcelain that is comparable to Western goods. Because it is cheap and good, it has indeed won a lot of glory for the national goods industry. So we invited five friends to visit the "Lihuo Brand Porcelain" Manufacturing Institute - China Enamel Factory. Led by a Mr. Wang, he explained it to us very clearly.

We first walked into the blank making workshop. This is the place where the initial work is done. The iron sheet is made into various models of blanks on the blank cutting machine. There is also an acid washing room and a raw firing room. The blank is washed with dilute acid and then refined in the raw firing place.

The powder making workshop can also be divided into five places. This is dedicated to making enamel powder. At the first place, the whole piece of stone is placed in a rolling machine and rolled into fine powder. At the second place, the technician will match the various raw materials to the required materials. The third place is to put the matched fine powder in the kiln for forging and burning, but in order to prevent the solidified fine powder from occurring after forging and burning, it is added with water at the fourth place and the water room. The fifth place is the storage place. We also went to the factory to visit. Many workers used dilute acid to wash the blanks clean. Secondly, a layer of viscous substance was applied on the blanks, and then a layer of enamel porcelain was added. Then it was placed in the fire for forging and burning three times. After forging and burning, it was added with flowers in the art workshop. This is painted with various colors to arouse the customer's love for beauty. There are three ways to add flowers: (1) Sticking flowers, (2) Spraying flowers, (3) Oil painting. In short, they are all made by scientific methods. After adding the flowers, it is forged and burned once. Then it can be packaged. However, according to Mr. Wang, they also need to conduct a strict inspection before it is released to the market. We know that crude manufacturing is on the road to extinction. Factories that work hard on national goods will not be like this.

Many of their raw materials are taken from domestic products, such as sulfuric acid, soda ash, and feldspar. However, there are several types, such as iron sheet and cobalt oxide, which still have to rely on countries such as the United Kingdom and the United States. This point needs to be paid attention to by the government!

The factory has about 300 workers, who work very diligently. It can be seen that great attention is paid to the training of workers at ordinary times. When I walked out of the gate of the China Enamel Factory, my heart was full of happiness. Mr. Wang's last words were still in my ears: "In the fifth year of the Republic of China, the total number of foreign enamelware imported into China was about 5 million yuan per year. Now, almost all of it is used by national goods."

— Binghun

Letter to the Editor: My humble work "Improving Coarse Paper" was published in the National Goods Weekly on July 18, which has attracted much attention from those engaged in the grass paper industry. However, the symbols in the equation are misplaced, and the addition is mistaken for multiplication, which has led to questions. Please correct them as follows:

The original draft of the first formula is translated as potassium dioxide, carbon dioxide, carbon dioxide three, light dioxide plus calcium dioxide is equal to calcium carbon dioxide three plus two parts of potassium dioxide (ie caustic potash)

The original draft of the second formula is translated as calcium (light oxide) two, plus two parts of sodium green is equal to calcium green two, plus two parts of sodium light oxide (ie caustic soda)

Those who inquired in the letter said that the second formula was impossible, but in fact, salt leachate also contains magnesium green two and magnesium sulfur oxide four, which are easily decomposed in caustic potash solution. Its green is attracted by caustic potash, so it dissociates and becomes an electrolytic ion. Therefore, the material must be heated during cooking, which is the same as the principle of electrolysis.

Also, it is proposed to add a note above the sentence "If it is filtered with a bamboo sieve to form a cake" (If rice straw is expensive, add one jiao per hundred jin, then add only five yuan per ton. If other materials are used, the same applies.) The reason is that the price of raw materials varies from place to place. Some people who sent letters said it was impossible, but in fact, the price of grass is at most two jiao more expensive, which is only thirty-four yuan per ton, which is not done, not impossible. The reason for the lack of prosperity of my country's industry is due to the hoarding of raw materials, which is very annoying! Tian Xu I am born with respect.

The International Trade Association held a symposium on the 23rd to discuss the development of China's foreign trade and its procedures.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 216

— (Pian Yue)

Walking with a bowl full of soup, focusing on preventing the soup from spilling, holding the bowl firmly with both hands, staring intently at the soup, and walking slowly and carefully, still results in quite a bit of soup spilling out. If you hold the bowl level with one hand, focus on the road ahead, and casually take care of any potential issues, the result will definitely be better – sometimes the bowl is full and no soup spills out at all. Many things in life are like this: if you are overly concerned about success and failure and deliberately seek success, it is better to do things step by step without any worries, which is easier to achieve.

The word "present" in "presenting a report on unusual movements" and the word "order" in "ordering commendation" – if these class-dividing terms are used, the spirit of "officials in a republic are servants of the people" will ultimately be obscured and lost.

Various fresh flowers are kept in vases, which can make the room full of spring and make everyone happy. However, the water in the vase that keeps the flowers is poisonous enough to kill people. When people appreciate the precious vases and beautiful flowers, how can they care about the hidden dangers in the contents! Throughout history, those who have been obsessed with female beauty and ultimately suffered from it have only seen the vases and flowers in their eyes.

The Method of Concentrating the Mind 217

— Tianxu Wosheng

All the joys and sorrows in life are created by the mind. If one can take a step back in one's thinking, one will realize that there are others in the world who suffer even more than oneself. In situations that are beyond one's control, even death may be unattainable, as in the unjust imprisonment of Yue Fei. Try to put yourself in their shoes and imagine, what would you do if you were to suffer the same pain? Dwell on this thought until death, and even beyond. This will illuminate the mind with great brilliance. Not only does the physical body not belong to me, but even the mind does not belong to me. The thought of "I" is what creates the "I." If the mind is without thought in sleep, then there is no "I." This is evident in the use of hypnotics for surgery. The "forgetting" in "sitting in oblivion" (坐忘) comes from "death" and "mind" (亡 and 心). "Death" means "nothingness." The "breath" in "regulating the breath" (調息) comes from "self" and "mind" (自 and 心). "Self" means "original." Originally, there was nothing. All that is seen and heard arises from nothingness. People may attribute it to Heaven, but in reality, Heaven itself is also originally nothing. All the winds, clouds, thunder, rain, sun, moon, and stars come together naturally, just like human affairs. They are not controlled by the will of Heaven, with its preferences and rejections. Therefore, I believe that the term "natural" (自然) is more fitting than "Heavenly" (天然). Rather than listening to Heaven, it is better to listen to nature. To "listen" means to perceive with the ears and create sound, which is still created by the mind. If the mind is not present, then one hears without hearing. Thus, the realm created by the mind exists only in a single thought. The character "thought" (念) comes from "now" (今), and "now" is just a single instant. Monks chanting the name of Buddha are chanting the two characters "not person" (弗人). Instead of thinking of oneself as a person, they only think of themselves as Buddha, thereby extinguishing all thoughts of suffering. Reciting the Heart Sutra (心經) means thinking about the path that the mind must take, crossing from this shore to the other shore. The "other shore" means escaping the present situation and imagining a transition. Like death, the physical body will inevitably decay, so why cherish it? Those who are oppressed by hunger, cold, and suffering are merely enslaved by the physical form. Therefore, I created the theory of the "mind's electricity," using a radio receiver as an analogy. The sounds broadcast in the air are not controlled by me, but I can choose to accept or reject them. The human mind is indeed more powerful than the mind of Heaven. Therefore, one who dislikes the sound of crying can immediately change direction and seek laughter and joy. If it is not satisfactory, one has the right to turn it off and stop it. However, if the direction is uncertain and wavering, it will create a chaotic sound, merely disturbing one's own mind. Therefore, I believe that the method of concentrating the mind lies only in the single character "stop" (止). All other explanations are merely superfluous words.

The Female Secretary of a National Hero 218

— Jin

The late Polish national hero, General Józef Piłsudski, dedicated his life to fighting for his country's salvation, and his achievements are well-known throughout the world. Anecdotes about his life are scattered in newspapers at home and abroad, all of which are worthy of admiration. Piłsudski strived for his country's independence and freedom, and advocated for gender equality. During the revolutionary process, the secret military organizations under Piłsudski's leadership all had female divisions, responsible for assassination, sanitation, propaganda, and military administrative liaison work. During the European War, Polish women were even more active. Piłsudski's wife was then the intelligence director of the First Brigade of the Polish Volunteer Army. Their friendship developed into marriage. Therefore, after Poland's restoration, men and women were completely equal, with female members of parliament, female senators, female members of various political parties, female scientists, artists, writers, musicians, etc. Miss Ira Kowalska, Piłsudski's private female secretary, is one of Poland's most famous female writers. Last year, she won the Polish literary prize, worth about four thousand Chinese dollars. Miss Kowalska is famous for writing domestic narrative novels. Her writing is concise and detailed, seemingly plain at first glance, but with endless aftertastes. Her descriptions of daily life and personal character are particularly comprehensive and captivating, resembling the style of the Dream of the Red Chamber. Miss Kowalska was born in 1891 in Wilno, Poland. She studied at Kraków and Oxford University in England. During the war, she also served in Piłsudski's Volunteer Army as a frontline nurse, repeatedly receiving medals. From 1918 to 1926, she worked in the Polish Ministry of Foreign Affairs. When Piłsudski regained power and became the Minister of Military Affairs, she was transferred to the Ministry of Military Affairs to serve in the military and concurrently as Piłsudski's private secretary. Many important documents and telegrams were written by her and widely circulated. Miss Kowalska's first work was completed in 1912. In 1930, she won the literary prize of Wilno. In 1933, she was elected as a professor at the Polish Academy of Literature, but she declined due to her military position. Last year, she received another military medal. She was highly valued by Piłsudski. Miss Kowalska's literary fame was enhanced by being the secretary of a national hero, and she was praised throughout Europe, becoming a celebrated story in the literary world.

Misty Records of Imperial Incense 220

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

"Where is this... I... I can hardly believe it, I really can hardly believe it." My father kept lamenting like this, saying it over and over again, I don't know how many times.

Even the Empress Dowager also felt that this was an unbelievable thing! After she hurriedly read those documents, she commented on them with Prince Qing as if in casual conversation. At that time, I was listening with my ears cocked, and I actually understood every word.

"We can't understand it no matter what," she said, "Someone like ××, born of such noble origins, and relying on the blessings of his ancestors, associating with nothing but princes and nobles, his position could not be higher; moreover, the imperial court trusts him so much, entrusting the military and civilians of the entire province to him, who would have thought that he would do so many scandalous things? This is really hard to believe! I don't believe that someone like him, if he had a clear head and put his conscience in the middle, would do any disreputable bad things; it is clear that his head is too muddled and his conscience is not in the middle, that's why this happened!"

The Empress Dowager's saying "conscience in the middle," explained in modern terms, means first, loyalty; second, integrity; third, trustworthiness; and fourth, a kind and benevolent attitude towards everyone.

Next, the Empress Dowager specifically raised the charge of his condoning his servants to whip a beggar to death for discussion. (374)

Local Customs and Notes

Japan, A Self-Confessed Earthquake Country 222

— Jiyun

Having lived in Japan for less than half a year, I have already experienced more than a dozen earthquakes. And because of the great earthquake in Taiwan last month, all Japanese residents are uneasy and worried about a major disaster looming. Japan has a great military force, but it can absolutely not stop earthquakes. There are also countless brilliant scientists who are immersed in research, but there is still no good industry for forecasting and preventing it. Newspapers say, "Japan is a famous earthquake country, and three or four minor tremors every month are a normal phenomenon. Although there have been six earthquakes in June, general observations show no unexpected danger, and residents do not need to worry." How can these irrelevant words reduce people's fear? Because in fact, the smoke from Mount Asama has not yet been extinguished!

When I first arrived in Japan, I really wanted to experience an earthquake and see how it felt. Because since I was born in China, I have never encountered an earthquake. The opportunity suddenly came. On the day of the great earthquake in Taiwan, it was around one or two in the morning, and I was awakened by the earthquake. The house shook very violently, rattling as if it were about to collapse. My body trembled up and down, left and right, as if I were on a train. At the same time, my head was slightly dizzy, like seasickness. I wanted to get up and take refuge, but there was no sound of birds outside, so I had to endure it. When I saw in the newspaper the next morning that there had been a slight tremor in Tokyo, I was startled. This kind of earthquake, which is extremely rare in China, is not a big deal in Japan and doesn't need to be fussed about. From this, it can be seen that the time of a strong earthquake must be very frightening.

Even a slight earthquake makes us restless on our pillows. I don't want to experience a stronger earthquake again. In the museum, I saw a train locomotive from the time of the earthquake, burned into several iron rods. Ironware and glass were melted into lumps. If it were humans, they would surely be reduced to flying bones and scattered ashes, without a trace. But after several earthquakes, I have gained some scientific experience. I feel that the vibration of an earthquake, like a ripple, has a pattern of expanding from the center point (epicenter) to the surrounding area. It becomes circular. The farther away from the center point, the weaker the impact, until it disappears. Moreover, this kind of ring-shaped vibration wave, sometimes strong and sometimes weak, is also the same as sound waves. Therefore, an earthquake can be divided into several times in the middle. Most of the time, I experience six or seven movements in ten minutes.

In places with many earthquakes and volcanoes, the earth's crust is thinner, so tall Western-style houses cannot be built. The soil in Japan is also loose, and the passage of streetcars and cars makes the houses and land on both sides vibrate. The tallest buildings in the country are nine stories high, and the state restricts them from being built taller to avoid danger. Therefore, they have to develop underground. Most of the larger buildings have basements, which serve as public dining halls. Recently, a certain company in Marunouchi (street name) is building a seven-story building. It uses compressed air to inject into the ground to consolidate the foundation. Who knew that the ground in the nearby people's houses would spew out foul odors. It was later discovered that the air injected underground by a certain company was spraying out in all directions because the soil was too loose. It carried underground impurities, so it became a slightly toxic foul odor. After opposition from the neighbors, construction was suspended. Japanese people want to compete with Europe and America in everything, but only in buildings can they not show their strength. They often envy Shanghai, which can build twenty or thirty-story buildings.

Nine out of ten ordinary houses are made of wood. There are no bricks in the walls, only wooden strips nailed together, with some gray sand or cement painted on the outside. So the appearance is very beautiful artificial stone, but the inside is mud and straw. There are no walls or partitions in the house, only thin doors covered with cloth, and the window frames and doors move to both sides. The delicate wooden strips can be broken with some force. The walls around the house are also mostly wooden boards. So it is easy to burn in case of a fire. Fortunately, Japan pays great attention to fire prevention, and people's homes generally have fire extinguishing liquid, so there are not many cases of dozens of houses being burned.

Because of the frequent earthquakes, the tiles on the roof are only one layer and are very thin. Recently, zinc is popular, which can reduce the weight even more. Their houses are not connected to the foundation. Wooden frames are placed on top of the foundation stones, and the houses are built on the wooden frames. If a crane is used to lift it up, it can be moved or changed direction at will. We live in the attic in Shanghai, and we often complain about the heavens and the earth. Who knew that the houses in Japan are all like birdcages. Because of the problem of living, they are often threatened by earthquakes, so they have to seek development abroad. This is also an important reason.

Free Talk

On "Critiquing Books and Critiquing People" 223

— Jun

After reading Mr. Lingjing's article "Critiquing Books and Critiquing People" in "Free Talk": "As long as the critic (reveals that they know more about the author than the book can tell them, their denunciation immediately becomes an attack, and their ridicule becomes an insult." I quite disagree. Mr. Lingjing thinks this statement is quite "correct," but in my opinion, it is not very correct. Mr. Lingjing believes that "the responsibility that a writer should bear when writing an article or reading a book is, strictly speaking, only the article or the book itself. No matter how wildly promiscuous, gambling, base, or despicable the author's daily life is, the critic should only look for "toxic" or "beneficial" elements in the book. As for the author's behavior, the critic doesn't need to worry about it. Social morality and national laws will naturally impose sanctions." It seems that Mr. Lingjing agrees with "evaluating the work based on the work" and does not agree with "evaluating the work based on the person" and "evaluating the person based on the work." But in fact, things are probably not that simple. Right now, we can see a group of self-proclaimed lofty hermits "whose hearts are the same as merchants," as well as scholars who are like "a lone crane in the clouds, flying back and forth to the prime minister's office, everywhere "scrounging for favors." When they open their mouths and pick up their pens, they are always talking about "unrestrained," "unfettered," and "free-spirited," making grand pronouncements about reality and fiercely scolding everything that is base and dirty, as if they are the only "noble" ones in the world. In society or in the "literary circle," we also often encounter a body wrapped in a tailcoat with second-stage syphilis, righteously denouncing people's prostitution? At this time, the critic has no choice but to "evaluate the person based on the person" or "evaluate the person based on the work," stripping him naked and letting the audience see what he really is. Because if you are still polite and "evaluate the work based on the work" at this time, then you will fall for his trick. He might even secretly laugh at you as an "A.Q." This is why people today should not be too honest, and "treating people with sincerity" should be based on the other party's attitude. Moreover, there are too many people with "double personalities" now, and comparing "words" with "deeds" has become an indispensable weapon. Therefore, "evaluating the person based on the work" and even "evaluating the work based on the person" are often unavoidable. Not long ago, we encountered those well-fed and well-clothed Beijing-style famous scholars who scolded people who write for a living for "having low character and low literary style." At this time, he does not treat you "sincerely," but you stubbornly want to treat him "sincerely." In the end, you always suffer. As a result, not only is it impossible to treat him with sincerity, but it is also impossible not to treat him with sincerity. So, when it comes to "treating people with sincerity," it is best to see the opponent clearly. If they are not worthy of being treated with "sincerity," then everyone doesn't need to bow and scrape and be polite. It's not too late to treat him with "sincerity" until he also treats people with "sincerity." In short, you can't just be "sincere" all the way. On this point, I agree with "treating a person in the same way they treat others."

Two Female Types (Part 1) 224

— Qi Wuwen

By chance, I circled around the north again. Judging from the train cars on the three northern lines, the third-class carriages of the Beining Railway are indeed a bit different from those on the Jinpu Railway or the Pinghan Railway. They are filled with "lowlifes" living inhuman lives—dirty farmers and simple small merchants. But here, there are already some "upper-class society" figures decorating it, and there are also Japanese and Korean faces interspersed among them. Therefore, even the length of the backrests and the height of the chair backs are decent. Take my surroundings as an example: next to me is a Korean woman with a flat face dressed in Chinese fashion. Sitting across from me is a middle-aged man in a Western suit. From his burly figure, prominent cheekbones, and stiff northern accent, I know that he is also Korean. The other one is Chinese—a young woman in her twenties. When I entered the station, she was running behind me, catching up to ask me which concession the ×× Hotel was in Tianjin. Her face is thin and has the color given by anemia. Her deep-set and dark eyes, and the scarred bridge of her nose, suggest that she is a precocious woman who has experienced worry. Her attire is ordinary student attire—a gray cloth qipao with an old raincoat, short socks with mud stains, and wide-toed flat leather shoes. Besides a small hand-carried soft wicker basket, she brought nothing else.

After we sat down, she continued to ask me whether she should get off at the old station or the new station. Then she automatically explained to me why she was going to a hotel in Tianjin:

"I'm going to Tianjin to find my brother. My brother had a fight with my sister-in-law and left home in a huff. My father isn't free, so I have to make a trip." Her accent is a typical Beijing female student accent, speaking very quickly. When she speaks, the muscles in her face and mouth move vigorously, expressing herself a bit too much.

Besides asking her how she knew where her brother was, I only replied with a hm-hm.

"His friend sent us a telegram." When she heard me speaking with a southern accent, she asked me where I was from. After I told her, I felt embarrassed not to ask her where her home was. She told me that she was from Jiangxi, but had lived in Beijing for many years. Her father worked in the Social Affairs Bureau in Beijing. She had also "stayed" in Shanghai for some time, and had only been to Tianjin once. Then she went from the differences between northern and southern dialects to issues such as northerners being dirtier than southerners.

I've never met a young woman like this who starts talking to strangers as soon as she meets them. Although I didn't get to the bottom of it, I didn't dislike her. I just felt that she was a bit different, but at the same time I felt that she was natural. In front of her, I was ashamed that I was showing the shyness and unnaturalness of a woman. But she didn't notice this and continued to talk to me intermittently. —Yes, she had also tried to strike up a conversation with the Korean woman sitting next to me, but because she didn't understand Chinese, she had to talk to me alone.

When a vendor selling cigarettes and candies passed by, she bought a pack of "Hong Xibao." She rummaged through the basket for a long time before taking out two dimes to give him. She first offered me a cigarette, but I repeatedly declined, saying that I didn't smoke.

"I thought you smoked, that's why I bought it. I don't smoke myself," but later she smoked several herself.

Good News 225

— Ye Zi

My sixty-three-year-old mother, my wife suffering from lung disease, and my two frail, malnourished children, threatened by famine, floods, and a heartless environment, fled miserably from our hometown more than three thousand *li* away, hoping to rely on me, their son, husband, and father, whose monthly income from writing was only a little over ten *yuan*.

As soon as we arrived, they were busy recounting the hardship in our hometown and taking medicine.

Because an elder sister with four or five children was left behind in our hometown, my mother would always sigh with an expression of being quite content with her vagrant life:

"We are still doing alright! Although it's hard, the whole family is together! … Only your sister, I don't know if their settlement has collapsed or not? Such a family that can't survive! … She should have written a letter long ago…"

Bending her withered fingers, she counted: six days, eight days… How many tears she secretly shed behind our backs, my wife and I didn’t know—longing for that letter of safety.

One morning, during heavy rain, my mother stayed up all night praying to Buddha for my wife's heavy coughing and cries of pain, and then fell asleep. The mailman delivered a letter from the back door with postage due, and after paying him eight *fen* in copper coins, I hid in the kitchen annex and hurriedly opened it.

The handwriting was blurred, and both the envelope and the paper were made of straw paper. Even before reading it, I knew the contents would definitely not be good. The words were not written with an ink brush, nor with a pencil, but perhaps with a charred twig. I remembered playing a game with my sister in childhood, writing with charred twigs, and maybe she hadn't forgotten and improvised it.

My hands were shaking as I read the letter, still worrying about my mother and wife waking up. The child had already started crying, so I picked her up and put her beside me, giving her a pair of chopsticks to play with. As I read the letter, the child tapped the washbasin with the chopsticks, singing a begging song popular among famine victims from our hometown.

The settlement, as expected, had collapsed. My sister's letter was written while crouching on a stone in the barren hills. She said:

“…That night, it was dark and without light, and the heavy rain almost broke through the roof. Your brother-in-law was called out by the gong to the dyke to rescue it, and I huddled in the middle of the main room with the five children, trembling as we waited for good news from those defending the dyke… We were not the only family not sleeping all night, but they were all burning incense, striking chimes, and crying out to Heaven to beg the bodhisattvas for help! …The dogs and livestock were howling, as if they knew a great disaster was imminent, searching everywhere for a place to settle… I tried my best to stop the children from crying! But the sound of gongs and rain grew louder and louder… Just as dawn broke, suddenly, from who knows where, there was an earth-shattering sound, and the floodwaters surged into our rice paddies and main room like an avalanche…

‘I don’t know what words to use to tell you about our suffering. In short, at that time, as soon as I saw the water, I cried out as if I had seen the messengers of death from hell! The children clung to me, and I couldn't run out the door to ask for help, and no one was willing to save us! Your brother-in-law couldn't come back either… In an instant, the water rose as high as the benches!… I carried the children one by one to the raised floor. You know our raised floor, it's only made of two planks… At noon, the water sealed our doors, and the raised floor was level with the water, so I could only dig open the roof and get the children onto the roof!…

‘The rain was still heavy, and we had nothing to shield us from the rain, and the wind was howling, and the waves sometimes reached as high as our roof. Our wet bodies waited until the sun came out to dry, sunburnt and dizzy, sunburnt and aching!… We endured on the roof for three whole days!… It wasn’t until the morning of the fourth day that we saw your brother-in-law coming in a broken rowing boat… One of the children, the youngest, died in my arms. Another—the third—Junxiang, was swept into the water by the waves at some point during the night! Perhaps he fainted from hunger and rolled into the water, without making a sound!…

‘Now, brother! I don't want to recount my suffering again. In short, you can imagine everything. You have experienced many floods yourself… We have now been transported to this barren mountain, which is full of disaster victims. Perhaps there are others among them who are suffering even more than we are! They are waiting all day for the relief officials to fly down from the sky. But for me, all hope is extinguished, because I have experienced too many floods, although this one was more severe than any other!…

‘Your brother-in-law hasn't had a drop of water or a grain of rice for five or six days, and he is burning with fever! But he said to me: "Go! Take the two youngest children and beg for food in Shanghai! You have studied and can read, maybe your brother can think of a way to help you!… Leave the older children to me, I only need to get a little better to catch fish!…" Brother, what can I say to answer him? I know. You yourself may not have a solution! Mother, your sick sister-in-law, and two children, and you have no job. Besides, we are not allowed to leave the region to beg for food…’"

As I read the letter, my nose stung, but I desperately tried to hold back my tears. My wife's coughing grew heavier, and I carried the child upstairs. My mother had already gotten up again and was pouring hot water for my wife. As soon as she saw me, she asked:

"Is that the letter? You were reading it downstairs…"

"Yes!" I said. Unable to hide it, I put the letter on the table; pretending she couldn't read, I said calmly, "It's good news from my sister. Their settlement didn't collapse!"

"Good news? Amitabha! …Heaven doesn't disappoint those who have a good heart!" my mother said, clasping her hands together, "Read it! Read it to me! Read it word by word!"

Forcing myself, I read aloud, and I felt that what I saw in my eyes was not straw paper, but a vast expanse of water, heaps and heaps of corpses of disaster victims! Among them were my sister, nephews, and even myself! But what came out of my mouth was a completely opposite, bountiful, unimaginable world. I said:

"She said, 'Tell Mother not to worry, thanks to the joint efforts of the officials and the people, our dyke didn't collapse!… Now the early rice is ripe, and I have harvested more than in any other year. The children are all very healthy too’…"

"That's great!" my mother smiled.

In the afternoon, I secretly wrote a reply, saying a lot of hollow, comforting words that didn't scratch the surface of the pain, and used the last three *yuan* that I had borrowed to buy medicine for my wife to buy a postal money order.

"Maybe they won't even receive my three *yuan*!" Walking out of the post office, I suddenly thought sadly, and tears could no longer be held back.

Chang'e's Make-Up Exam 226

— Yao Xueyin

After publishing "The Chinese Goddess of the Sun and Moon," I was bored during my illness, so I opened my reading notes and found that I had missed a lot of materials, which I greatly regretted. Among the most important were two items, the first of which is: Gao You had already said that Chang Yi became Chang'e. In "Lüshi Chunqiu Reviewing and Distinguishing," there are two sentences: "Xi He made divination of the sun, and Shang Yi made divination of the moon," and Gao You annotated:

"Shang Yi is Chang'e, so read Yi as He, and later generations had the vulgar name of Chang'e."

Regarding the earliest record of Chang'e flying to the moon that I have seen, it is in "Huainanzi Lanming Xun." The book "Huainanzi" was written by a group of alchemists, so the story of Chang'e flying to the moon is obviously a fabricated story, not a myth. In myths, people seem to have only known that rabbits or toads lived on the moon, and did not know that there was a Moon Granny. "Heavenly Questions" says:

"What virtue does the nocturnal light possess that it is reborn after death? What is its benefit that there is a hare in its belly?"

This is a myth that probably prevailed in the Jing and Xiang areas during the Warring States period. In Mexico, Zululald, and Tibet, there are similar stories. "Huainanzi Jing Shen Xun" says:

"There is a three-legged crow in the sun, and there is a toad in the moon."

"Shuo Lin Xun" also says:

"The moon shines on the world, eating in Chan Zhu."

Chan Zhu is a toad. It is also a toad. "Lüshi Chunqiu Ji Qiu Ji" says:

"The moon is the root of all Yin. When the moon is full, the clams are full, and the Yin is full; when the moon is dark, the clams are empty, and the Yin is lacking."

This myth is probably differentiated from the former one. This is treating the moon as a clam, the full moon is the full clam, and the dark moon is the empty clam.

According to the two sentences in "Reviewing and Distinguishing" that I cited, we also know that Xi He transformed into divination of the sun at the end of the Warring States period, and Chang Yi transformed into divination of the moon. However, Xi He was regarded as the sun driver, but Chang Yi was not regarded as the moon driver. The moon driver is a god called Wang Shu, only seen in the Chu Ci, which must have been a legend from the Jing and Xiang areas. Chang Yi has made divination of the moon, which is the second material I missed in the previous article.

Secondly, what should be added is: the moon's sisters (or brothers) are twelve, implying that this myth occurred after the twelve months were clearly divided, so it is thought to be no earlier than the Yin and Shang dynasties.

University Days (30) 227

— Written by German Storm, Translated by Chen Yin

The flowers have passed; now the road is no longer lined with elm trees, but with slender, tall birch trees. After walking for a while, I came to a cool forest, which grew straight up a hill on the left; on the other side, I could see the sea through the trees. In the densest part of the forest in front of me, there was the silver bell-like singing of thrushes and the charming calls of black cranes. In addition, I heard the rustling of leaves and the sound of sea waves surging underneath, like music. I suddenly remembered a half-old house, also in this forest. A few years ago, when I was still a sophomore, I came out of school to visit a college student who was related to me, and I went there with him. As far as I knew at that time, the house was built by a hotel owner who was engaged in speculative business; later, the speculation failed, and he could not attract many customers to this secluded place, so he had to sell the house. The new owner of the house only sent a servant to take care of the sparse business.

I still remember that the servant was a pale-faced, tall man; the single-story building was hidden among the towering birch trees on the hillside, and now it appeared very clearly in my mind. My first glass of Grog was still drunk under the small colonnade in the center of the front of the house, and from this colonnade, through a double door, one could reach a tall and dark hall, with windows facing the forest behind the hall. At this time, I became interested and wanted to revisit this secluded place, but at the same time, I was worried that the house no longer existed or could not be found.

As I was thinking this, I looked up and saw a narrow path winding up the hill from the left side of the road through the trees. I stood for a while, remembering that it was the same at that time, so I slowly walked up the hill along this path. After walking for a while, I saw a gray sloping roof appearing among the leaves in front of me, and slowly I could also see the tops of the two windows under the columns of a small colonnade. After a few more steps, a wide staircase led me from the shade of the trees to a flat little square.

The house stood before me in the secluded sunlight in the middle of the forest. Long time no see, it seemed that nothing had changed. The original light pink painted walls, in the part near the ground that had not peeled off, were still covered with green moss, just like then; the cracks in the wooden columns were filled with brown grass cores; now there were still two dark green benches on either side of the half-open double doors under the small colonnade. — I sat on a bench, watching the sea below through the gaps in the trees, at which time a fishing boat was sailing across the sea illuminated by the sunlight. — It seemed that no one lived here, everything was quiet; no sound came from the house behind me; only a wild bee flew past buzzing, and two black butterflies were flying in the grass beside the stone steps.

Germany Rearrests Jews 228

— Xing An

Since Hitler came to power in Germany, an anti-Jewish movement soon occurred. At that time, Jews living in Germany suffered significant oppression. Some were exiled, some were imprisoned, and some were insulted. Afterwards, the National Socialist Party was quite satisfied, and the trend calmed down.

However, before the Jews had time to recover from their shock, Germany is now carrying out a second anti-Jewish movement. Moreover, the tension is even greater than the previous anti-Jewish movement.

This time, Germany's rearrest of Jews has become a widespread trend throughout the country. Disturbances have occurred in various places, and there have been several incidents. The other day, a movie theater in the western part of Berlin was showing an anti-Jewish film, and the Jewish people in the audience all hissed and left their seats, causing a riot. In addition, several National Socialist Party soldiers had a conflict with Jewish people walking on the street. At one point, the usually magnificent Kurfürstendamm was filled with noise. The National Socialist Party believed that the street was the center of the Jewish people, so they shattered many pieces of glass in the shops opened by Jewish people. At the same time, anti-Jewish incidents have also continued to occur in other cities.

Regarding this German rearrest of Jews, public opinion in various countries has been critical. However, according to General Daliu Qi, commander-in-chief of the German police, the German anti-Jewish movement is very legitimate. Daliu recently presented a detailed statistics of Jewish people committing crimes to the press, stating that based on the statistics, the number of crimes is the highest among Jewish residents. Foreign public opinion often cannot understand the German anti-Jewish movement. If foreigners could understand these statistics on Jewish people committing crimes, they would not only not side with the Jewish people, but would also pay attention to the crimes of the Jewish people in their own countries. And Xi said that the Jewish people who cause trouble live in Germany as if they were eating the land. But they don’t know how to be grateful for their residence. To the point of forgetting why they are here, they do not know how to examine their behavior at all, which is strange.

Alas, Jewish people eat the land but do not know how to repay the depth of kindness and sing praises, and they still do not know how to check themselves and repeatedly violate criminal laws. The Jewish people really do not know what time it is.

In Sickness 229

— Jingyun

When the nurse, with her neatly combed hair, came in to check my temperature for the last time, I lay in bed, uttering a weak, trembling voice, anxiously asking:

"Miss Shi, how is the temperature today?" How eager the desire to live!

"It's much better already. — But now you need to rest fully to calm your brain nerves; at night, don't let your mind wander." After saying that, she put the thermometer into the box and walked out of the room with a slight smile.

The air in the room was like that of a monastery, silent and solemn, and even the throbbing of my pulse could be heard faintly.

The sounds of insects singing chirped and chirped at the base of the wall, and the moon poured in through the window, its silvery light exceptionally bright and clean. Her silky silver light permeated the entire house, all the way to the depths of my heart lying on the bed, making it as clear and bright as the moon. This lonely and peaceful situation is like a mother's comfort to the patient, caressing an uneasy heart like the calm water lake in the deep mountains surrounded by peaks, calm without the slightest ripple of waves.

I lay flat on the bed, gazing foolishly at the silvery white moon shadow slowly crawling on the pale white wall. At this time, I did not feel depressed or lonely at all, but my heart felt suddenly enlightened. Everything is floating clouds, and so-called wealth and fame are just a wisp of ethereal smoke to life, so what is there to cherish? In the turbid human world, why should I try to gain advantage by scheming and fighting? I am deeply grateful that this minor illness has allowed my heart to abandon all the busywork and calm down. In this lonely and peaceful environment, I can close my eyes, calm my breathing, and leisurely savor some past events.

In fact, a person in the depths of illness will not always be so foolish as to think about those smoke-like fame and wealth, because he is gradually walking towards the realm of death, separated from the ghost by only a closed door, and there is always the possibility of entering. At this time, his heart is the most enlightened and peaceful. When he looks back on some things in the past, he will naturally feel amused and foolish in secret. If someone were to put fame and wealth next to his bed at this time, asking him to risk his life to fight for it, then he may not have such great courage; and what remains in his heart at this time is probably only a strong and urgent desire to live.

Years ago, when I was in the South—Siam—I also entered the Chulalongkorn Hospital of the royal family for treatment because of an illness. Whenever the sun collected its scorching rays, like a salted egg yolk resting on the treetops in the west, I leisurely dragged my light steps to the green lawn in the garden, sitting on a chair under the umbrella-like banyan tree, casually admiring the golden afterglow on the brilliant and sparkling spire of the Buddha "Viet" (temple), and the red clouds in the blue sky, and the flocks of small birds chirping and chirping back to their nests. At that time, I often met a middle-aged man with dark brown skin, a strong body, and an age of about twenty to forty in the garden, dragging a cane and circling on the grass, quite heroic, looking really unlike a patient. Soon, the two lonely patients finally struck up a conversation. Then I learned that he was an active military officer—a very famous colonel, who had been admitted to the hospital for treatment of neurasthenia.

"...With such a strong body as yours, and being a military officer, it doesn't seem like you should have this disease," I said. Speaking in a somewhat impure foreign language.

"Mr. Yun, (Mr. Yun) what is the difference between literary and military? A person's life is intoxicated by fame and wealth. For the so-called future of wealth and fame, who doesn't rack their brains to scheme and fight?..."

Several loud and heavy bell sounds were sent from the Buddha Viet, and the dim shadows of dusk seemed to be ambushing soldiers, slowly spreading out from all around.

"Life is just like this, wealth and fame are just a fleeting dream. It's better to be a carefree monk," he closed his eyes tightly, like a monk meditating in front of a Buddha statue.

Thinking of the colonel's words, I turned off the bedside lamp, and a bottle of lilac flowers on the windowsill was reflected on the pale white wall by the moon. I stared foolishly at the beautiful flower shadow on the wall, and fell asleep with a calm heart.

One of the Pleasures of Living in the City 230

— Tan Tan

For people living in the city today, unless they are millionaires who can build an acre of garden on Jing'an Temple Road or Yu Yuan Road, salaried workers with limited monthly income really do not have the happiness of enjoying the vitality of a blade of green grass. In fact, this is entirely because they don't know how to arrange it themselves. If they put in a little effort, then even people with a monthly income of forty or fifty *yuan* can get some "flowers and trees."

I have planned it in detail, and I will write it below to contribute to the people living in Shanghai.

Of course, people without clothes and food are now flooding the city, and my plan is only for the sake of a few people.

First of all, we must choose the location to rent a house. In the downtown area, the rent is expensive, and there is too much noise, which often destroys the peaceful air. What is particularly important is that the lights are too bright at night, you stand in the courtyard and look up and you can't see a single star, and the moonlight like water will never soak your bitter steps.

If you don't have the ability to live in the entire building, it is best to find a way to rent the downstairs living room. Because if you rent the living room of a single building, the small courtyard will undoubtedly belong to you. This immediately removes about one and a half to two feet of the cement floor on both sides of the small courtyard. With a little manpower, it becomes two very good "medicinal railings." Then plant a very large rose flower in the corner of the right wall. Roses are very easy to cultivate, and at the same time, they often bloom. With this one, even when other flowers are not blooming, it will not be lonely. Plant a crabapple tree near the rose, whether it is a weeping crabapple or a Chinese quince. With its smearing of scarlet red, you can deal with this brocade-like spring. In addition, as long as you plant one or two more canna lilies and balsam in this medicinal railing on the right, there will be flowers to see in the hot summer and early autumn. On the left, a *Nandina domestica* cannot be forgotten. It is an evergreen tree, and even in the severe cold of snow, it is green and lovely. Camellias, like coral-like seeds and the same root, make a bleak winter very lively. Of course, cotton roses cannot but be planted. His appearance of melancholy in the wind and dew is really the soul of autumn, and the blue begonias in the cracks of the wall can brew a strong autumn flavor in the late autumn with melancholy rain and wind. With these kinds of flowers and trees, there are decorations in all seasons of the year.

In the spring, the windows are wide open, and the spring scenery in the courtyard is for me to write and paint. In the summer, you must not forget to hang green bamboo curtains outside the long windows. It can not only isolate the sunlight and heat, but also give you the pleasure of being immersed in water. On autumn evenings, the courtyard is filled with moonlight, and the cool dew drips. A weaving lady on the balsam keeps calling. You turn off the lights in the room, and look out from the bamboo curtain. The canna lilies are graceful in the wind and lovely. At this time, you lean on the sofa, pour a cup of bitter tea, and sip it slowly. At this time, the scenery is really unknown whether it is poetry or a dream. In winter, it is best on a snowy night. You close the windows tightly, letting the cold light of the accumulated snow reflect from the glass. When there is wine, you sip the wine. When there is no wine, you can sip boiled water. If there is a stove, you naturally start a fire. If there is no stove, you wrap the thread quilt around your body.

The best is of course a rainy day, especially the continuous autumn rain. Friend, you may not know the benefits of a rainy day. It makes you secluded, it makes you quiet, it makes you deep. Of course, it will also make you sad, but this sadness is light and vague. At this time, it is best to lie idly on the bed, reading books that do not cost money. When you are tired, put the book aside and look out of the window to see the thin strands and strips of drizzle falling patiently and weakly. The begonias can't stand even this drizzle, and they hang their heads and think deeply. At that time, you can also follow him to think, from world affairs all the way to life until you are too hungry to get out of bed in slippers and go somewhere to eat.

The Sorrow of Old Age 231

— Dan Er

The nursing room gradually became desolate and quiet. Even the heavy cough of the old man in the nursing room, usually heard, couldn't be heard by the children outside the house this early spring.

The village had become quite chaotic in recent years. The old man of the nursing room, Second Grandfather, once regarded as the most respected, had been forgotten by the villagers in recent years. Especially the young people, sometimes encountering him by the door or in the alley, didn't even feel like saying "Third Grandfather" or even nodding. This old man's uneasy later years were compounded by an indescribable pain, making his face always anxious, gloomy, and rarely speaking. This spring, he finally fell ill from accumulated worry and suffering, which made him even more sorrowful. How could the villagers not even know about his serious illness? No one came to inquire.

One spring, the old man had a nightmare of going through the gates of hell. He was certain he would die this time, but he was still alive. Moreover, he was even able to leave the room and sit on the armchair in the center of the hall, which he hadn't touched for months. As soon as he sat down, his thirteen-year-old daughter was about to massage his back, but he already felt a burst of soreness all over. Clearly, it was caused by some emotion.

The old man stared with blurry, unfocused eyes, silently looking at the courtyard in front. Many star fruit tree leaves were scattered there, rotten star fruits turned black, withered black star fruit branches, desolate, enveloped in a layer of decaying and desolate atmosphere. He slowly shifted his gaze, and on the dilapidated black tiled roof opposite, a lonely wind that made the old man's heart tremble lightly blew, sweeping through the leaves of the star fruit tree in the lazy courtyard, faintly rustling in the quiet. The old man's heart was like a string about to break, plucked by something that made him unbearable.

He sighed deeply, thought deeply, and felt the emptiness of life, and felt a terrifying sorrow. His painful old age would decay in loneliness, dying in solitary desolation! He couldn't see any of his five sons. Tears welled up, seemingly regretting that he didn't die this time. This time, he still had two sons to send him off to his death! He would see it even more in the future...

The three sons in Nanyang, because the store went bankrupt, didn't send money, and even lost contact. The fifth son escaped after a disaster and wandered abroad. Their mother burst into tears whenever she thought of them. The third son's teacher also said he couldn't be relied on. The village was uneasy, banditry was pressing in, and rent couldn't be collected from the fields, and selling them was impossible. The whole family was women and children, how could they survive! Moreover, people came to demand debts, saying they would arrest people in the opposite house. It had changed so quickly in just two or three years, it felt like a dream! The old man felt pain and strangeness. He didn't know what to do. He seemed to have fallen into a terrifying deserted valley, a deep abyss. This was nothing like the gentle, peaceful home of a few years ago! He was trapped in all sorts of terrible thoughts, and all his withered muscles were trembling.

He was entangled in a coma from a serious illness for more than a month, making his daughters-in-law and daughters complain. The eldest daughter, who was relatively wealthy and whose husband's family had moved to the city, said in the old man's delirium: "Father has no hope, better to withdraw the blessings sooner, so as not to exhaust the children..." This clearly meant that they hoped their father, who was useless and exhausting them, would die sooner. The old man overheard this. How could people's hearts be so bad, in this world, even children are like this...

Fortunately, in the midst of near death, he saw his long-separated third and fifth sons. Their return made their father feel a little better, his mother said. However, after only ten days or so, the father's pain became dangerous, but the countryside was already in turmoil, many villagers had fled from the banditry, and at night they listened in terror to the... the terrifying, ear-piercing cries of the villagers. And finally, while the father was in a coma, the two sons left, abandoning their critically ill father!

The old man's forehead, full of wrinkles, felt like someone was stabbing it with a knife. His head hung down, and in a tearful voice, he asked the little daughter beside him: "Are the bandits better now?... Did your brothers say anything when they left..."

"The bandits came to Xiapu again last night, and even captured people..."

"Help me into the house..." The old man's unbearable sorrow was so painful that he couldn't support himself...

Rambling Words 232

— Qin

My old friend Huang Suqiu, a wild talent from Yun, excels in calligraphy and painting, surpassing ordinary people. Once he puts his pen to paper, he has no regard for others. However, he is full of complaints and laments, and never likes to scold people with words. He often says that scolding oneself is self-respect, and scolding others is not only self-deprecating, but people will also laugh at me for being narrow-minded. I remember that in the early years of the Republic of China, he inscribed on a painting imitating Mei Hua'an Daoren (Taoist of the Plum Blossom Hermitage), "Some praise me for being a triple excellence, but I call myself having four excellences: talented but unrecognized, living off an empty mountain, no way to appeal, and wife and children worried. This is called 'absolute door, absolute road,' revealing all the secrets of heaven, wearing out the iron inkstone, the mountain spirit angered, the demons rejoiced, taking away his lifespan, overturning his ancestral temple. This is called 'absolute descendants.' But if there was a Mei Hua'an in the previous life, I would definitely follow the Taoist." He inscribed on a painting imitating Shi Tao, "Poetry, calligraphy, and painting all imitate Shi Tao. The courtyard is desolate and lonely like a monk, the brushstrokes are bleak, the connoisseurs are few, the orphaned life is the same as that of the blind Venerable." He also wrote a couplet for himself, "Raise your head to peek beyond heaven and earth, lose your footing and fall into the world of poetry and books." At that time, he was indulging in drinking and wildness in his hometown, full of depression, occasionally venting in inscriptions, but never uttering a word to defame anyone. After the Gengshen year (1920), he made a living painting in Shanghai, and became even more secretive and self-critical, his wild demeanor completely restrained. (Que Chou)

"News Reporter"

After firing blanks for two days, only today can there be real bullets.

News 237

Qiyin Opera Society, now expanding its business, is recruiting male and female members. Anyone who is interested in opera during their school days and has a clean background can join. Letters can be sent to No. 19, Lane 842, North Chengdu Road, including a 4.5-inch half-length photo and a resume, one each. It is also heard that the society will broadcast programs on the Huaxing Radio Station this Sunday.

Movie News

Diantong News Line 238

Wang Ying's first vocal performance in Diantong's "Zishanshen" (Mountain God) on the screen. According to recording engineer Zhou Bo, her voice is bright and clear, so her pronunciation is particularly clear.

Lan Ping is participating in the re-performance of "Nora" while also handling the work of the Diantong Half-Monthly Pictorial, facing both sides, she has become a busy person.

The Diantong basketball team has recently been divided into two groups, A and B. Group A is named the Big Heavenly King Team, and Group B is named the Little Heavenly King Team. It is heard that the Guangzhou Gongping Daily basketball team is coming to Shanghai for a visit, and the Big Heavenly King Team will invite the team to play a game.

Gu Menghu left a deep impression on the audience in "New Woman," and also made an excellent cameo in "Autumn Fan and Bright Lamp." This time, in Diantong's "Freedom God" directed by Situ Huimin, everyone said that his acting was seasoned, truly worthy of being a versatile actor.

Yesterday, Wang Ying, Chen Boer, Wu Mei, Lan Ping, and photographers Wu Yin Xian and Chen Yao Ting went to Zhao Feng Park for a drive. Against the exquisite background, the two photographers took many excellent works.

Microphone Broadcast 239

Zheng Zhengqiu signed Qin Haha's folding fan on the tenth of this month, and fell ill on the evening of that day, so Qin's folding fan signature became a posthumous inscription.

Hu Die's starring role in "Tuberose" has not yet been completed due to her trip abroad. After returning to China, she was busy with banquets and Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu's funeral. Yesterday, director Cheng Bu Gao set up the unfinished scenery and started work.

It is said that the young photographer Chen Chen resigned from the Mingxing authorities yesterday because he had not had work for a long time, and went to Hankou to engage in activities.

Photographer Zhang Jinde was exceptionally busy for Zheng Zhengqiu's funeral, and the photos in the "In Memory of Zheng Zhengqiu" special issue of Mingxing Half-Monthly are all from Zhang Jinde.

The first sound film produced by Jixing Company, "Difficult Sisters," was well-received when it was screened in Beijing.

Shen Xiling, Wan Guchan, Li Shu Zhi and Chang Shao Bai took a car to Diantong Company for a visit yesterday and were quite satisfied. Zhou Bo Xun hosted them.

— Guan Zhen Photography

Yi Hua Intelligence 241

Yue Feng's "Dr. Wife," originally scheduled to start filming on the 15th, Yue has given up this plan due to certain relations and has compiled a script with new subject matter and stimulation.

In "Hero of the Times" there is a miscellaneous play in the flour exchange, in which several people posing as brokers are specially invited by director Ying Yunwei from his broker friends in the city's flour exchange, so the results of this scene were filmed extremely well.

Ying Yunwei told people that the script for "Hero of the Times" began to be written during the production of "Peach and Plum Tribulation," costing several times more effort than "Peach and Plum Tribulation."

In "Triumphant Song" there is a Dragon King Temple, where more than a hundred large and small Buddha statues in the temple are carved by many craftsmen specially hired by Yihua to sculpt statues. Twenty-five large Buddha statues, twelve medium Buddha statues, and thirty-nine small Buddha statues have now been completed. The largest Four Seas Dragon King statues will begin to be carved in the next few days. These craftsmen specializing in making statues said that before carving, they must first wash their hands and burn incense, otherwise they will inevitably suffer from headaches and fever. Who knew that the Buddha statues used in "Triumphant Song" were used to remove superstitions.

Publishing Industry 242

The fifth issue of Diantong Half-Monthly Pictorial is published. The cover and back cover are portraits of Lu Luming and Gu Menghu. The text includes Wang Ying's letter to the innocent world, Xu Xingzhi's theory of complete composition, Elmer's Hollywood from stage to screen, Ruby's Chinese from stage to screen, Swan's flirtation between stage and screen, Wu Zhi's Diantong life, and Bai Ke's scenery of July 14th. The images include thirty-three photos of Chinese people from stage to screen, a page of Hollywood people from stage to screen, and the scenes of "Freedom God," a corner of urban scenery, and two amusing comics and captions. The Diantong Pictorial, which is constantly improving in each issue, will be published by the editorial department in collaboration for the sixth issue, a special edition of "Freedom God."

"Movie Fan Weekly" has resurrection news: This publication is known for its "special news," so after its suspension, many people clapped and applauded. It is now heard that it will meet readers in the middle of next month. The resurrection issue has as many as eight "special news" items.

The cover of the inaugural issue of "Movie News" is a mink-spotted new swimming suit. It is said that the origin of this photo is not small, and the editors of the publication are very proud of it.

Composer Nie Er Dies Tragically 243

Microphone news: Film composer Nie Er drowned in Tokyo after being swept into the sea by a huge wave while swimming. His body has not yet been recovered. Lianhua's "Fisherman's Song" and Diantong's "Children of the Storm" were both composed by him. The film industry has lost another artist.
